I'll explain so others know how to use this: ***<br /><br />In most places, you will need to bend/curve the device for use, though the degree in which you bend the device depends upon the location it's being used the the type of hair to be removed. I've personally found that over the upper lip, only a slight bend is needed, whereas courser hairs might need a much stronger bend. Then, simply roll the device in the direction opposite the hair's growth. On most of the face, including over the upper lip, simply rolling it upward will get rid of the hairs. Sometimes, with more stubborn hairs, the device will need to be placed at an angle before use, depending upon the hair's growth.<br /><br />Cleaning is a cinch. Simply bend the device to remove the hairs and use soap/water when necessary. Dry thoroughly.

  747. I was skeptical about this product and it does take a while to actually arrive. I have been tweezing for years on a daily basis and hate it. The trick (as mentioned from other reviews) is to curve the spring into an upside down U shape, press it to your skin with the pink ends down and then roll the ends away from your face. It will hurt but it does get better. It is quicker than tweezing and gets the little hairs better. I still tweeze any missed hairs, but there are only a few!
